## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillations / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where the restoring force and/or damping are nonlinear functions of position x and velocity v, possibly with time-dependent driving. The equation of motion follows Newton's second law with nonlinear force terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping dependent on position)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (harmonic external driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing with driving)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (position-dependent stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity-dependent friction)
- General polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (asymmetric restoring force with damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve oscillator symmetry; even powers (x**2) indicate asymmetric potentials
- Velocity-dependent terms linear in v represent viscous damping; terms like v*x**2 indicate amplitude-dependent damping (van der Pol type)
- Sinusoidal functions of time sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicate external periodic driving forces
- Sinusoidal functions of position sin(c*x) suggest a periodic potential (pendulum-like systems)
- Products of position and velocity (x*v) can arise from non-conservative or gyroscopic-like coupling terms
- The sign of the cubic coefficient relative to the linear term distinguishes hardening (same sign as linear) from softening (opposite sign) springs
- Parametric excitation appears as multiplicative coupling between position and periodic time functions: x*cos(c*t)
- Absence of explicit time dependence indicates an autonomous system where energy is conserved or monotonically dissipated

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.0884*v³ - 0.1959*v*sin(x) - 3.998*x³ - 0.1959*sin(v)`

The key terms in the GT are:
1. `x³` term
2. `v³` term
3. `v*sin(x)` term — this is non-polynomial in x
4. `sin(v)` term — this is non-polynomial in v

Most candidates are polynomial in both x and v, so they cannot produce `sin(x)` or `sin(v)` terms. Let me look for candidates that contain trigonometric or transcendental functions.

**Candidate 26:** `c0*x³ + c1*v + c2*sin(c3 + c4*v) + c5*v*x + c6*v*Abs(v) + c7*v*x³`

This has `sin(c3 + c4*v)`. If c3=0, c4=1, this gives `c2*sin(v)`, which matches the `sin(v)` term. But we still need `v*sin(x)`, which isn't present. The candidate has `v*x` and `v*x³` but no `v*sin(x)`. So this can approximate `v*sin(x)` only polynomially (via Taylor: `sin(x) ≈ x - x³/6 + x⁵/120...`), but not exactly match it. **No match.**

**Candidate 38-41, 46-48:** These contain `exp()` terms, not `sin()` terms for x. Let me check candidate 46:

**Candidate 46:** `c0*x³ + c1*v + c2*v³ + c3*v*exp(c4*x) + c5*v*x*Abs(x) + c6*sin(c7 + c8*v)`

This has `sin(c7 + c8*v)` which can give `sin(v)`, and `v*exp(c4*x)` which cannot equal `v*sin(x)`. **No match.**

None of the candidates contain a `v*sin(x)` term explicitly. The GT requires both `v*sin(x)` and `sin(v)`. Let me check if any candidate can produce these through some algebraic manipulation.

For `v*sin(x)`: The Taylor expansion is `v*(x - x³/6 + x⁵/120 - ...)`. A polynomial in x multiplied by v would need infinitely many terms to match this exactly. No finite polynomial can equal `sin(x)`.

So I need a candidate that either:
- Contains `v*sin(x)` and `sin(v)` explicitly, or
- Contains terms with `sin` that can be configured to produce both

Looking through all candidates again carefully — none contain `sin(x)` at all. Candidate 26 and 46 contain `sin(v)` (via `sin(c + c*v)`), but no candidate contains `sin(x)`.

Could `v*sin(x)` be produced from any non-polynomial term? Looking at candidates with `Abs`, `exp`, `x**c` terms:

Candidates with `x**c4` (like 18, 19, 31, 33, 34, 43): These give `v*x^c4` which is a power function, not `sin(x)`.

Candidates with `exp(c*x)`: exponential, not sine.

Candidate 42 has rational functions of x, but rational functions can't equal `sin(x)`.

**Conclusion:** The GT contains `v*sin(x)` and `sin(v)` terms. No candidate formula contains `sin(x)` in any form, and while some contain `sin(v)` terms, none can reproduce `v*sin(x)`. Since `sin(x)` cannot be represented as a finite polynomial, rational function, exponential, absolute value, or power function, no candidate can be made equivalent to the GT.

- `sin(v) ≈ v - v³/6 + v⁵/120 - ...`
